HAWAI'I LODGING & TOURISM
ASSOC lAT ION
January 6, 2022
Aloha Councilmember Paltin,
We, a coalition of tourism, business, and labor organizations, are appealing to you to
request your consideration in voting to sustain Maui Mayor Michael Victorino’s veto of Bill 148
which would create a moratorium on the issuance of building permits for all new lodging
1
accommodations throughout Maui. We are aware and concerned about the intent of the measure
that was passed by the Maui County Council. We believe strongly that Bill 148, as it is currently
written, will not have the intended effects sought by the Council and will inadvertently hurt not
only Maui’s overall tourism industry, but also have negative effects for countless other
businesses that rely on tourism to employ thousands of Maui residents.
For instance, Bill 148 does not adequately address the proliferation of illegal, short-term
vacation rental units—an issue that begs for more attention and prioritization. As we are all well
aware, the most explosive growth in visitor accommodations in recent years has not been in the
traditional, brick-and-mortar lodging operations, which have been nominal, but in short-term
vacation rental units—both legal and illegal. Unscrupulous operation of illegal units has led to
the unchecked growth of short-term rental inventory in both resort and residential zoned areas.
Ease of booking, relative price, and their availability have drawn travelers to these units, and this
will continue and likely worsen if the development of traditional lodging properties is limited.
Curtailing development and restricting growth will only drive more visitors to these
accommodations and will further exacerbate the need for more affordable housing for local
residents.
It also remains our position that a moratorium on building permits will have the
unintended effect of depressing the market for other sectors of the economy including the
construction industry as well as other various skilled trades—many of which rely upon the
tourism industry for their economic well-being. The issuance of building permits ultimately
means more projects, more jobs, and more opportunities for Maui residents; limiting this for our
economy on the heels of a worldwide pandemic is self-destructive and will have lasting
economic consequences for Maui County. Meaningful and substantive investment into Maui’s
economy could be jeopardized or lost.
It is a substantive fact that tourism remains Maui’s strongest economic driver. It
consistently provides jobs not only in the lodging industry, but also in ground and air transport,
activities and attractions, retail and dining, the service industry, and the agricultural sector which
provides local goods and produce for eateries enjoyed by visitors and residents alike. Putting a
two-year hold on building permits will effectively hamstring the industry as it works to attract
the ideal traveler and provide a quality experience on the Valley Isle, hurting our overall tourism
product and creating new challenges and roadblocks that will need to be addressed in the future.
Finally, we would be remiss not to cite the last-minute changes that were made to Bill
148 just prior to its passage. This did not allow for proper vetting and for a robust public
discussion to take place. A measure with such staggering impacts on the local populace and
economy deserves more openness and transparency, and this measure was not given the
appropriate time to be considered by the public in any meaningful way.
In closing, we would like to reiterate that we understand that the people of Maui are
seeking well-thought-out solutions to strike a balance between the needs and desires of local
residents and visitors. We remain steadfast in our belief that Bill 148 is not the answer. We,
therefore, stand ready to work with the Maui County Council to identify alternate strategies to
address better tourism management, so at this time we ask that you consider the ramifications of
this measure and vote to sustain Mayor Victorino’s veto.
Mahalo for your consideration.
2
He*,Mull Hunnemunn
President & CEO
Hawaii Lodging & Tourism Associalion

Testimony of

OFFiCE Or THE
COUNTY CLERK
Maui County Council
Council Meeting
January 7, 2022
Chair Lee and members of the Council, mahalo for the opportunity to submit testimony on behalf of the
Hawaii Lodging & Tourism Association, the state’s largest private sector visitor industry organization.
The Hawaii Lodging & Tourism Association—nearly 700 members strong, representing more than
50,000 hotel rooms and nearly 40,000 lodging workers—recognizes that the intent of this measure is to
place limitations on the overall numbers of travelers that visit Maui on any given day, but remain
convinced that Bill 148 is short-sighted, will not lead to a more responsible and respectful tourist to
travel to Maui, and will have unintended and significant ramifications for the countless local business
that rely upon tourism to employ thousands of Maui residents.
As HLTA has stated repeatedly in every part of the state, it has become glaringly clear over the past
several years that the explosive growth in transient accommodation units is not occurring in traditional
lodging operations but in short-term rental units—both legal and illegal. This has happened in both
resort and residential zoned areas, and Maui residents continue to suffer the consequences. Limiting the
expansion of resorts while not enacting clear measures and oversight of short-term rentals will
ultimately drive more travelers to these units and will place further stress on Maui’s affordable housing
market. We believe this is where more emphasis needs to be placed by government and a collaborative
effort made with the private sector and labor groups to make our neighborhoods more affordable for
local residents. We stand ready to work with the Council and Mayor Victorino’s administration to
identify alternate strategies to provide both better tourism management and an adequate inventory of
affordable housing for Maui residents.
Moreover, a moratorium on building permits will depress the market for other sectors of the local
economy including skilled trades of all types—many of which rely upon lodging properties for the bulk
of their work. Allowing building permits to be freely issued to legal lodging operations means more job
opportunities for Maui residents and placing limitations on the county’s overall economic recovery
seems self-destructive and unnecessary. This will have lasting consequences that will lead to the loss of
meaningful and substantive investments into Maui’s economy.
Maui relies upon tourism for its economic well-being; this was evident throughout the COVID-19
pandemic. The industry brings people and money to the island, and residents enjoy jobs not only in the
lodging industry, but in retail, dining, activities and attractions, and even the agricultural sector which
counts tourism among its most consistent customers. Enacting a moratorium will ultimately hurt this
industry and, by extension, the countless Maui residents who comprise its workforce.
Hawai i l,odging Tourism Association
2270 Ralakaua Avenue. Suite 1702. llonoliiiu. Hawaii 96815 ● I’hone: (,808) 923-0407 ● Kax; (808) 924-3843
infoat hauaiilociging.org ● www.liawaiilodging.org
Finally, it must also be noted that significant changes were made to Bill 148 just prior to passage which
did not allow for the robust public discussion that a measure like this deserves. Legislation that would
have far-reaching effects on the local populace deserves transparency, and the final changes to Bill 148
did not have the time for public scrutiny or discussion.
For these reasons, HLTA opposes Bill 148 and asks the Council to vote to sustain Mayor
Victorino’s veto.
Mahalo for the opportunity to provide this testimony.

Resolution 22-4, East Maui Water Leases:
“I support the Proposed resolution to have State and County control over east Maui water, and I am against
irrevocable 30-year water leases for Mahi Pono. We need autonomy over our own water. And it should not be
delegated into private hands. Our water is a public resource. The waters of Hawaii are held as a public trust. I
support the Council adopting the Resolution “on the floor” of the Council meeting, rather than referring it to a
committee”.
Resolution 22-5 on Red Hill,
As a watershed advocate, I Support Efforts "URGING THE UNITED STATES NAVY TO PERMANENTLY REMOVE AND

Item CC 22-9 the Visitor accommodation Moratorium override^:
We have taken a lot of our time and your (councilperson’s) valuable time to come up with this bill. We cannot
allow the Mayor to veto our hard efforts and undermine the democratic process. That is why we are asking you
to overturn this unjustified Veto.
Maui is sick, from an imbalanced tourism industry. We are overrun with too many tourists and have far
exceeded our island’s capacity. Too much of our water goes to the Hotels and resorts while local
families cannot get water meters, and we have water restrictions.
More land is being sold to developers for Timeshares. Condos, and Hotels. While we have an extreme
housing shortage, and an affordable housing crisis.
The tourism industry is not suffering from Covid, Corporate profits from tourism are. Airlines are
complaining and hotel chains are complaining, about recouping all of their lost profits, But hotels are
actually more profitable now than ever before, even if their occupancy is slightly down.
We already do not have enough Locals to fill the jobs in Tourism. Hotels and Tourism businesses often
have to bring in more staff from the mainland or overseas to fill local jobs.
While our own people have to more off island because of hieh costs of living. The tourism industry does
employ a lot of local people, but big corporations like hotels are not willing to pay the locals a living
wage. So they often recruit mainlanders to do the lowest-paying jobs. They know that they can get
cheaper workers short-term But the wages they are paying are not sufficient to support a local family
long-term. Low wages are unsustainable in the long term.
1
Maui’s minimum livable wage needs to be above 20 dollars per hour for a young single person, and
higher for anyone with dependents. How many hotels are already paying this “minimum livable wage'
to all of their housecleaners and support staff?
There are too many Cheap Flights and Too Many Hotel Rooms: This keeps prices low and increases
demand. More heads in beds, and more travelers, will require more cheap labor necessary to service it
all.
Building more hotels creates more competition among existing hotels, and reduces demand for existing
hotels/beds, and the value of a room drops.
When the value of a hotel room drops, there is less money to pay cleaners and maintenance staff, as
cheap labor becomes increasingly necessary to maintain the increasing number of rooms.
In fairness to our workforce: Our workforce needs to clean/service fewer rooms for more money.
Building more hotels will not help us to achieve that. Building more hotels at this time will create an
economic disincentive for hotels to pay higher wages to local workers. This will cause them to seek out
mainlanders and international workers.
Hotels are not ('always') built bv local workers: Hotels are often built by off-island work crews.
Interisland or mainland companies are brought in. In short, these Hotels are not being built to help us
or our community, they are being built to exploit our resources and labor force.
Our Island is severely out of balance over-tourism and we need this Moratorium to help control the
excessive growth of tourism and restore some security for our community and our economy. Please
overturn this Veto.
Mahalo,
David Dorn

From: Dick Mayer <dickmayer@earthlink.net>
Sent: Thursday, January 6, 2022 6:53:59 PM
To: tampaltin@gmail.com <tampaltin@gmail.com>; Tamara A. Paltin <Tamara.Paltin@mauicounty.us>
Subject: Over-ride the Mayor's Veto
Aloha Councilmember Tamara Paltin,
Mayor Michael Victorino has again shown his interest in promoting a bigger Maui tourist industry. He
vetoed a well-considered County moratorium (passed 6-3) which would temporarily limit even more
tourist accommodations over the next two years.
The Maui Island Plan provided guidance for the council and the mayor. He decided to ignore its
provisions which recommended, “To protect the quality of Maui’s visitor industry, and the island
lifestyle, the County must carefully manage and control any future expansion of visitor units on Maui
island." (MIP Page 4-11); and “Mitigate the impact of tourism on the host culture, natural environment^
and resident lifestyles.” (MIP Page 4-13)
The mayor gave as his rationale for allowing even more growth that his departments are unable to
enforce the law against illegal vacation rentals, even though voters approved a $10,000 fine for any
illegal vacation rental. If the mayor's reasoning is accurate, how can a tourist from far away find an
illegal vacation rental so easily, while the mayor's local administration is unable to locate illegal
rentals?
It is unfortunate our mayor feels it necessary to bring in more tourists and put even more rental cars
on the roads when our infrastructure is not capable of handling the existing impacts. Furthermore,
Maui's world famous and highly respected tourism industry is jeopardized by further
expansion. It will erode the product that Maui is trying to market.
When any of the construction trades come to you and say that you hurt construction jobs, you will be
able to say this opens up the opportunity for the construction industry to upgrade the quality of all of
our existing and aging tourist properties while constructing amenities, room improvements,
etc. There should be lots of jobs.
1
Let’s protect what we have; not let tourism overwhelm us. The Council should override the Mayor’s
veto.
Mahalo from Maui’s residents, Dick Mayer
dickmaver@earthlink.net

REC EDTESTIMONY OF JEROME KEKIWI, JR.
PRESIDENT, NA MOKU AUPUNI O KO'OLAU HUI
Ml JAN -5 PN 18RE: MAUI COUNTY COUNCIL RESOLUTION NO. 22-4
URGING THE MAYOR TO ENTER INTO AN INTERGOVERNMENTAL AGREEI^^^^i^V^'i ^WITH THE STATE OF HAWAII BOARD OF LAND AND NATURAL RESOURCES TO
PROVIDE A LONG-TERM, RELIABLE, AND AFFORDABLE SOURCE OF WATER
FOR COUNTY DOMESTIC AND AGRICULTURAL USE
January 7, 2022
Aloha. My name is Jerome Kekiwi Jr. and I am the President of Na Moku Aupuni
0 Ko'olau Hui. Our members are the lineal descendants and current residents of
Ke'anae-Wailuanui in East Maui. We grow taro, fish, hunt and gather to feed our
families as a way of life. We are the lead plaintiffs in the East Maui water cases,
including the June, 2018 decision that restored East Maui streams.
We would like to thank our elected Council member, Shane Sinenci, for his
strong leadership on this issue. We believe he has done as much as humanely possible
to do the right thing for his constituents. Thank you Councilman Sinenci.
In testimony before the Board of Land & Natural Resources last year on whether
EMI’s Final EIS should be accepted, we acknowledged the good work and relationship
that our community has recognized and developed with Mahi Pono.
However, we did express concern that the BLNR not turn over control of this
critical public trust resource to a foreign-based pension investment fund whose business
model includes aquisition of water rights both here and abroad, for profit.
We agree with this Resolution’s basic premise, which is that as fiduciaries, policy
and decision-makers, this Council is obligated to act foremostly in the best interest of its
constituents, who are also its public trust beneficiaries.
The truth is that for many decades our community suffered great injury,
acknowledged in both court and Commission on Water Resources Management
decisions, under Mahi Pono’s predecessor, EMI, as well as this County, who were allied
against us in our water struggles. Because of this, it is very difficult for our community to
side with either Mahi Pono or the County. What is proposed in this Resolution looks
good, but politics being what they are, and in spite of our best efforts, too often we have
seen good public policy, and practice, shift to the bad after an election. So we are
hoping that all of you who believe that public trust resources should be managed by
Hawai'i, and not foreign corporations, will continue to serve on this Council.
After many decades of fighting all the powers that be - the state, county, labor
unions, big corporations, their vast network of supporters, here is what our community
can say for certain.
Hawai'i’s public trust resources should be controlled by Hawai'i. It is dangerous
to surrender this trust obligation to a foreign for-profit corporation. Our disadvantaged
position relative to the global market is readily apparent with our housing crisis. Foreign
investors with unlimited cash are literally pricing local people out of their homeland.
What we want is community partnership, management and stewardship. It’s
going on four years since streams were restored in our moku and we have endeavored
to do all within our power and means to be good stewards. This is not a business
proposition for us, but one of sacred kuleana, and our community has been diligently
exploring various models and viable alternatives.
Our community's mission is to be good stewards of the land and its resources.
Whatever happens today, we would like to have a stronger and more cooperative
relationship with all the stakeholders, to work together to take good care of the land and
water. In the past, efforts at this have been blocked. We remain open to working with all
stakeholders to move forward in a pono way.
Thank you for this opportunity to testify.
#####

Karri Ayasanonda <karrija@gmail.com>

Aloha Maui County Council Members,
I am writing in support of the moratorium on visitor accommodations. Over the past recent years, the quality of life for
myself, family, and many other residents has been drastically reduced due to overtourism. Our communities are being
destroyed by tourism and poorly managed development. I have seen family and friends have to move away from Maui
due to lack of housing, lack of good education, and lack of decent healthcare. We have tourists in every
neighborhood. Going to the store or a doctor's appointment has become a headache with too much traffic and crowds
of people. We skip going to places we used to love because there is no parking or there are just too many inconsiderate
people. We are seriously outnumbered by visitors in most places we attempt to go. We no longer can go to restaurants
due to crowds. We are seeing people of the community move away, including teachers, nurses, doctors, and many
other much needed members of the community. Going to the beach is not relaxing as we watch swarms of visitors
trampling over reef and chasing turtles. It has come to the point that my family also is looking at where we can move
our family to that we can live our lives in some type of peace, somewhere that residents are treated better, somewhere
we do not have to constantly write letters and plead with legislators to do what is right. As medical professionals we
feel we deserve better, as does every other person that is part of the Maui community.
Maui does not have the infrastructure for the amounts of visitors that arrive on a daily basis. Tourism is not managed, it
is more of a free-for-all and the island has been overly commercialized. We do not need even one more hotel,
timeshare, or any other property type of accommodation for visitors. Maui needs to decrease the amount of visitors
now before the beauty and resources have been completely depleted and the culture has disappeared. P^se pass the
moratorium on visitor accommodations before it is too late. O i i

oMahalo,
Karri Ayasanonda RN

Aloha Maui County Council Members,
January 5, 2022
I am writing to support the moratorium on Visitor/Transient Accommodations that was passed by the County Council
and vetoed by Mayor Victorino. I request you override his veto. This moratorium is a small but important step in
regulating over-tourism that currently exists.
As an Emergency Physician, I can attest that the lack of housing and infrastructure has impacted the quality of life here
on Maui and becomes a deterrent in attracting and keeping much needed workers that range from healthcare
professionals such as doctors and nurses to those who are considered essentia! workforce.
The Maui Island Plan that recommends limiting tourism would help to provide homes and improve resident access to
our beaches, hikes as well as provide the infrastructure such as water that was rationed in order to provide hotels and
resorts an unlimited supply for pools and landscaping.
2022 is already seeing tourism return to the uncontrolled and unsustainable growth that was seen in 2019 where traffic
was obscene, natural resources such as hikes, beaches, and parks were abused and damaged. Mayor Victorino has
chosen to side with the uncontrolled aspirations of unregulated businesses that take away beach parking, cause severe
congestion on roadways such as Hana, and encourage mainland investors who have now driven up housing costs to the
point where local residents are forced from their homes to mainland locations where living is affordable.
Even as a physician who has lived on island since 2008, 1feel like a second class citizen and am considering leaving Maui
as well since the beauty and Aloha spirit that drew me here is waning quickly. It is replaced with congestion that rivals
the rush hours that remind me of Chicago with the road rage that 1 left long ago.
I am SO tired of having to write letters again and again and testifying again and again for something that seems so
common-sense. I am disappointed in our Mayor and will vote for someone with common sense and a vision to save
Maui. I hope the Maui council will act with this same common sense and desire I feel is needed to preserve what is left
on this once beautiful sanctuary now becoming a new Waikiki. 0
1

Ordinance 22-9
I strongly support a building moratorium of transient housing on Maui. We need
affordable homes for locals who are working and trying to survive by working 3
jobs and overcrowding their homes with family and friends who cannot afford a
home of their own. As the decision to drill wells in my moku for delivery to the
east side is being debated, the water issue needs to be resolved before adding
more visitor accommodations. That is where the County priority should be at this
time.
There are also unintended consequences by allowing transient accommodations to
continue unabated. To the quality of life, our limited natural resources and our
reefs.
I question how many workers in the building industry are brought in off island?
How many of these building contractors are from Hawaii? Employees brought in from
off shore are taking up valuable housing spots. Please veto the Mayors override.
Back to 22-6
I strongly support stronger oversight to the planning commission for cell phone
tower regulation.

showing up with little notice or without proper oversight on permitting on
private lands.

Wl JAN -6 AH 8- 17
Aloha Chair Lee and Council Members,
OFFICE OF THE
1 would like to take this opportunity to express my concerns bh BiH148'aTid why 1
support the mayor's veto. I am opposed to Bill 148 for several reasons; however, I
do support the intention of the Bill regarding the number of visitors that come to
visit Maui. Having experienced visitors with rude, unruly and with entitled
attitudes, I feel that there can be other ways to address this instead of a
Moratorium. I have heard comments from previous testifiers who support Bill
148, such as "The hotels have deep pockets so they can wait 2 years" however, in
1990's a Moratorium was passed by Mayor Lingle for new construction projects
for Maui County. The effects of that were detrimental to the Blue collar working
class community and affected mom and pop businesses that are no longer in
operation today. So, a Moratorium today, especially during the pandemic would
negatively impact Maui's economy. With a Moratorium, in 2 years' time there
will be many lay-offs, reduction in hours, and eventually some people will be
unemployed. We know there are a ripple effects from job loss - theft, illegal drug
use, domestic violence is just a few. We don't have 2 years!
It was mentioned that there would be alternatives that will assist our blue-collar
working-class members with new employment opportunities, but I have yet to
see or hear of anything being proposed. Just hearsay with no results.
It would be nice to see the mayor and council members working together in
finding solutions to what we are experiencing on Maui Island. Instead, there is a
lot of division between the county government that trickles out to the
community. Being born and raised in Maui, I now see that there is a "Old Maui"
and a "New Maui." I understand that many who came to Maui make it their home
but are always wanting change. They want to accommodate their lifestyle that
does not align the values of our "Old Maui" residents. We come from a
generation of plantation and cattle ranch workers. Visitor Industry workers and
construction workers. There was a time when Maui was able to sustain itself
when we had Haleakala Dairy, the egg farm, sugar cane, pineapples and HOTELS.
But "New Maui" residents settled in could not and did not adapt to the smell of
the dairy or egg farm or smoke from the sugar cane and called for the shut-down
of these industries. Unfortunately, now all we have are the Visitor industry,
construction industry and some cattle ranches and an ongoing need for
affordable housing. You can't buy a house without  agood paying job with steady
income.
It's time we sit down and break bread to find solutions. In conclusion, please
support Mayor Victorino on his Veto of Bill 148, not for him but for the engine
that drives this community-the working-class women and men of Maui county.
Dwight K Burns
Hawaii Operating Engineers Industry Stabilization Fund
Maui Island Representative

January 5, 2022
8RE: Bill 148, County Communication 22-9
Moratorium on Transient Accommodations
Email: county.clerk@mauicounty.us
Aloha Maui County Council Members:
I am writing this letter in support AGAIN of the moratorium on visitor accommodations on Maui, that
was passed by the County Council and vetoed by Mayor Victorino. PLEASE override his veto! This
moratorium is a crucial step toward remediating the current unregulated over-tourism we are seeing
here.
The Maui Island Plan suggests limiting the number of visitors to approximately 1/3 the number of
residents in order to preserve our environment, infrastructure, and quality of life for residents--all of
which would improve the visitor experience as well.
The year 2019 was already a year of uncontrolled growth, fueled by the tourism industry. Promises
were made by leaders during the early part of the pandemic to improve on the tourism experience for
both visitors and residents. Residents were promised that the goal would be to decrease the number of
tourists while protecting the islands. Since October of 2020, those promises have been completely
forgotten by our leaders, who proudly announce that the goal of reaching 2019 numbers has been met
and now exceeded.
The current volume of tourists we were seeing pre-pandemic and now, in 2021, during the pandemic, is
a threat to the health, safety and quality of life of the residents of Maui, our environment and wildlife.
Our island resources are very limited. Our inadequate sewage treatment, water, and landfills are not
meant for this level of use. We just finished months of a of a severe water shortage, yet only Upcountry
residents were affected, not tourists. While my family's yard dried up and died due to not watering it,
the hotels are literally sucking up water as if there is no restriction. While sewage is discharged into our
oceans, tourists are overcrowding our beaches and cruelly abusing our wildlife (1 am thinking about
honu and dolphins right now). Our fishing industry is endangered by the abuse the ocean environment is
experiencing.
On Maui, tourists do not stay in the tourist areas, but drive all over the island, causing huge traffic
congestion—and this is despite the rental car shortage. Tourists don't even think twice about using up
resources meant for residents, such as UHauis! I have seen horrific pictures of the road to Hana being
blocked by tourists who choose to park on the road, blocking traffic, because of lack of parking.
Residents are literally being told that we do not count and that the tourism industry is all-powerful. Our
mayor has not showed any support of controlling tourism, including vetoing the last proposed
moratorium for south and west Maui and vetoing the affordable housing bill. He goes out of his way to
please the big money brought in by the tourism industry and mainland investors. He has made it clear
that residents are second class citizens to tourists. It is the responsibility of government officials to
ensure that there is adequate affordable housing for those who are essential to making our community
work (health care professionals, teachers, police, social workers, restaurant workers, grocery/retail
workers and yes, workers in tourism), not to incentivize nonresidents' profiting off tourism.
Residents here sacrifice a great deal financially to live here and deserve to be able to enjoy the beaches,
hikes and parks. Instead, there is no room for residents on any of these. The majority of residents here
do not depend at all on the tourist industry—yet all of us are made to sacrifice for it. For me, it is about
more than a financial sacrifice, as this is not only my birthplace but also that of my ancestors.
Hardworking residents are trying not to chased out by greedy leaders who put short-term profit first.
Our economy needs to be diversified. Our children need to be taught skills that will help them to
succeed in society, rather than just to serve tourists. We need a moratorium on future visitor
accommodations while solutions can be implemented, including leadership that supports resident lives
over the tourism industry.
Residents are SO tired of having to write letters again and again and testifying again and again for
something that seems so common-sense. 1 am so disappointed in our Mayor, who despite being a Maui
Boy, so obviously supports the moneyed tourist industry over residents' quality of life. I voted for him
and feel terribly betrayed. He has sold us out, and 1 for one will do all I can to ensure that someone who
supports residents' quality of life will replace him in the next election.
I appreciate the members of the Maui County Council greatly. With few exceptions, you are the leaders
who put residents and the 'aina first.
Mahalo Piha,
K.a'1 liupcitA-te
Kai Duponte, MSW

Dear Mayor Viotorino:
SUBJECT: MAUI COUNTY BOARD OF WATER SUPPLY SUPPORT OF THE
COUNTY OF MAUI ACQUIRING THE LONG-TERM WATER LEASES
FOR THE NAHIKU, KE'ANAE, HONOMANU, AND HUELO LICENSE
AREAS
On December 16, 2021, the Board of Water Supply (BWS) received extensive
testimony from the public, as well as presentations from Maui County Managing Director
Sandy Baz and Maui County Council Agriculture and Public Trust Committee Chair Shane
Sinenci. Following the presentations and testimonies, and per the agenda, the BWS
discussed Recommended Immediate Actions (page 81) and the Recommended Near-Term
Actions (page 82) from the Board of Water Supply Temporary Investigative Group (TIG)
Report, which was approved unanimously by the Board of Water Supply on December 19,
2019.
The Board subsequently approved by unanimous vote, submitting this letter of support
to the Mayor and the Maui County Council, encouraging the County of Maui to pursue the
feasibility of acquiring the leases for the Nahiku, Ke'anae, Honomanu, and Huelo license
areas through an intergovernmental agreement with the Department of Land and Natural
Resources (DLNR), as recommended in our 2019 TIG Report. To this effect, the Board
recommends contacting DLNR as soon as possible to determine next steps for doing so.

Thank you very much for your time and consideration in this matter.

Dear Council Chair Lee and Council Members,
I will not be able to be at your virtual meeting tomorrow. However, 1 would like to make a comment on item CC-22-9 -
the moratorium on tourist accommodations.
First, I want to say that I have been on three community panels on the future of Maui County - Decisions Maui, Maui Nui
Task Force, and the General Plan Advisory Committee. A major concern for each planning group was that Maui County
would not be adversely impacted by overgrowth of Maui County. The common theme of the planning groups was to
keep Maui, Maui for the local people.
Second, the Mayor's argument that the moratorium "may encourage residential units into short-term rentals." This is
true right now and that is the reason that we have hired staff to oversee this problem to assure compliance with our
laws to prevent the move of residential units into illegal short-term rentals. We need to make sure
enforcement happens.
Third, Maui is a beautiful place and It is world famous as a wonderful place to visit and live. And people will want to
come here regardless of our policies. When I worked with the late Mayor Elmer Cravalho, his vision as shared with me
was that the tourists would be focused in specific areas - Kaanapali, Wailea and Kapalua and would be staying in hotels.
Allowing short-term visitor accommodations in residential communities was not the original vision.
In summary, I believe that the people of Maui County want us to reassess the original vision on how the tourism industry
will make life better for Maui County residents. And therefore, 1 ask you, the Maui County Council, to override the
Mayor's veto and take the next two years to reset the vision of how the tourist industry will make life better for the
residents of Maui County.
Thank you.
Stan Franco

January 6, 2022 HAWAII HOTEL/"*
^  -1 , _ .^FrlCE OF THE ' '
Councilmcrnbcr Alice Lee, Chair Q (j N1 C L ^ P
Councilmember Keani Rawlins-Femandez, Vic^ tnair
Members of the Maui County Council
Support of CC 22-9 regarding Veto of Bill 148 ("A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE
ESTABLISHING CHAPTER 19.98, MAUI COUNTY CODE, DECLARING A
MOIMTORIUM ON NEW TlUVNSIENT ACCOMMODATIONS ON MAUI")
Hearing date: Friday, January 7, 2022 at 9:00AM
RE:
Aloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and members of the Maui County Council,
My name is Jerry Gibson, President of Hawaii Hotel Alliance ("HHA"). I am testifying
in STRONG SUPPORT of CC 22-9 regarding a veto of Bill 148 which seeks to create an island
wide moratorium which prohibits the issuance of any permit under Title 19 for two (2) years.
We support the Mayors veto of Bill 148 due to the economic impacts of the moratorium and
share his concerns with the lack of public input on the substantial changes made at second
reading.
The purpose of Bill 148 is to establish a moratorium to reduce the number of visitors to
comply with visitor to resident ratio specified in Chapter 2.80B of the Maui Island Plan by pausing
the increase of transient accommodations. However, there is no evidence which indicates that
pausing the development of transient accommodations will decrease the number of visitors to
Maui. Bill 148 will not stop visitors from flying to Maui. Rather, visitors will continue to travel to
Maui and will seek out other accommodations even though transient accommodations are limited.
It is concerning that such a broad and inflexible policy would be implemented without first
showing transient accommodations as the primary cause of these negative impacts.
HHA agrees with the Mayor that visitors will seek accommodations in residential and
apartment districts further impacting local residents. For instance, visitors will stay in
accommodations such as the increasing number short-term vacation rentals ("STR"), which are
the fastest-growing segment within Maui's visitor accommodations industry. These STRs burden
residential neighborhoods and long-term apartment inventory directly impacting the quality of life
for Maui residents. The data shows that the number of hotel rooms on Maui has decreased by 16%
from 8,577 in 2000 to 7,251 in 2020, however, the average number of visitors arriving on Maui
per day rose by 25% from 2000 to 2015. Thus, it is clear that the increase in visitors to Maui is
directly correlated to the growing number of STRs. The moratorium fails to address the illegal
STRs that continue to permeate residential neighborhoods on Maui. If the purpose of the bill is to
ultimately decrease the visitor count, perhaps further regulation is needed on the number of illegal
short-term vacation rental units that are allowed.
In addition, as further detailed in the attached legal memorandum, HHA has legal concerns
with the proposed moratorium as it violates the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.
In short, Bill 148 is not rationally related to a legitimate state interest as Maui Island Plan 4.2.3 is
not unenforceable. Likewise, HHA shares the Mayor's concerns on the lack of public input on the
substantial changes made at second and final reading. The public was deprived of the opportunity
to weigh in on the amendments which included an alteration of the affordable housing exception
ratio.
Moreover, Section 2 as currently drafted is grossly unfair to existing projects undergoing
permit application review. Under Section 2 the moratorium will be applicable to permits currently
being reviewed that have not received their final discretionary approval. Essentially, applications
that have already expended a substantial amount of resources and time will be halted in the current
step of the application review process once tlie moratorium is passed. It is clear, the amended
Section 2 is patently unfair to applicants that have properly filed and applied for a permit prior to
the implementation of the moratorium. In addition. Section 2 as currently drafted undermines the
Planning Commission's recommendation that the moratorium not impact current permit
applications.
Furthermore, HHA agrees with the Mayor's position that Bill 148 will result in substantial
negative economic impacts for Maui County. The visitor accommodations industry provides
employment to thousands of Maui residents which make up approximately 75% of all private-
sector jobs on Maui. Bill 148 will result in the loss of much-needed employment opportunities for
local Maui residents who work in construction, tourism, and other related industries. In fact, if
such a moratorium is implemented, there will be a loss of hundreds of construction jobs and
hundreds more hotel jobs during the two-year period alone. For example, the proposed renovation
of the Grand Wailea which will be paused by the moratorium will result in the loss of:
215 construction jobs that will be created each year over four years, which generate
$46 million in earnings and $7 million in new state taxes.
1.
2. 245 additional permanent tourism jobs on Maui, equating to $12 million in
earnings per year and $2 million in state taxes. These jobs will be in key areas,
including management, food and beverage, accounting and at the front desk.
3. An additional $650,000 per year in property taxes paid to the County of Maui -
amounting to a 12.4% increase to the cuiTent $5.2 million.
4. Increased annual contributions from Grand Wailea to the newly established County
Transient Accommodations Tax and more than $20 million in Transient
Accommodations Tax revenue for the state.
The loss of new jobs and economic impact will be far more substantial with the prevention
of future transient accommodations. In turn the moratorium will contribute more to the outward
migration of local families.
Lastly, Bill 148 will discourage future capital investment in Maui. It is concerning that the
County would seek to implement policy that would deter future investment in Maui as the County
continues to recover from the COVID-19 pandemic. The County will risk forgoing substantial
amounts of future investments, tax revenues and job creation for Maui’s economy moving forward.
On balance, the unintended consequences, including the negative impact on our economy,
far outweigh any potential, yet unsubstantiated reduction in the number of visitors this moratorium
will cause. In addition, the identified legal concerns and lack of transparency justify the Mayor's
veto of the measure. Indeed, there are far more effective ways to reduce the amount of visitors on
Maui without such a far reaching measure. Accordingly, HHA respectfully asks the Council to
uphold CC 22-9 vetoing Bill 148.
Mahalo for your consideration.
3V
Jerry Gibson, President
Hawaii Hotel Association
SULLIVAN MEHEULAi LEE RECEIVED

A LIMITED LiABILTY LAW PARTNERSHIP
January 5. 2022
OKriCE OF THE
COUNTY CLERK
MEMORANDUM
TO: Hawaii Hotel Alliance
William Meheula, Esq.
Legality of Bill 148 - Maui County Visitor Accommodations Moratorium
FROM:
RE:
This memorandum summarizes the legal flaws of Bill 148 (2021), A Bill for An
Ordinance Establishing Chapter 19.98, Maui County Code. Declaring a Moratorium On
New Transient Accommodations On Maui.
Background
On Friday, December 3, 2021, the Maui County Council (“Council”) resumed
consideration of Bill 148, and adopted three amendments - two of which overruled the
guidance of the Maui Planning Commission - before voting to waive Rule 19c to pass
Bill 148 on final reading with substantive amendments.
As discussed in item 3 below, despite the recommendations of the Planning Commission
that the moratorium not apply to project applications that were deemed complete by the
Planning Department, the Council amended Section  2to apply to any project that did not
receive final permit approvals. The revised language has considerable due process
implications by halting projects that have been in development for years in reliance on
existing law. In addition, this substantial amendment was made by waiver of the
Council’s procedural rules and floor vote without further opportunity for public
testimony in disregard of Charter section 4-2(1) that requires two readings for a proposed
ordinance.
Substantive Changes Adopted by the Council on December 3
1. Section 19.98.040 (F) was amended to read: “Any development that includes
new housing units built, at a ratio of at least one housing unit for every one
transient accommodations units, rounding up to the nearest whole number, of the
total number of new transient accommodations.”
This substantive change reverts the affordable housing exception to the moratorium back
to a 1:1 ratio, overturning the recommended language of the Maui Planning Commission,
who had sought to maintain current County policy requiring developers of new vacation
accommodations to also provide new workforce housing units equal to at least 25% of the
total number of new visitor accommodation units proposed. A previous version of the
measure set the ratio at 1:3.
Pacific Guardian Center ● Makai Tower ● 733 Bishop Street, Suite 2900 ● Honolulu, Hawaii 96813
Phone: 808.599.9555 ● Fax: 808.533.2467 ● www.SMLhawaii.com
Mayor Michael P. Victorino
1/6/22
Page 2
2. Section 19.98.040 (F)(4) was amended to read: “the new affordable housing
units must be physically constructed or may be converted from transient
accommodation units.”
This substantive amendment precludes developers from purchasing credits to fulfill their
obligations under Section 19.98.040(F).
3. Section 2 was amended to read: “this ordinance takes effect on approval and
applies to any new transient accommodation that has not received its final
discretionary approval.”
The intent of the amendment is to clarify that the moratorium applies to applications
currently in the process of receiving a determination of final discretionary approval.
Chair Lee, joined by Councilmembers Sugimura and Kama, opposed the amendment
based on equity and fairness for applicants who invest significant time and resources in
preparing applications to the County that would allow for the construction of new visitor
accommodations. The opposing Councilmembers correctly noted that equity and fairness
were the basis of the Maui Planning Commission’s recommendation that all applications
filed prior to the effective date of Bill 148 should be exempt from the moratorium.
Bill 148 Violates Due Process
The third amendment violates the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment
because the Council misused the General Plan that was developed after input from state
and county agencies and the general public as required under Charter section 8-8.5 as a
means to eliminate the Planning Commission’s right to rule on hotel room addition
applications.
Here, the Council’s reliance on Maui Island Plan section 4.2.3 as its justification for Bill
148 is an improper misuse of or revision to the Maui Island Plan. Section 19.98.010
states: “The purpose of the moratorium established by this ordinance is to comply with
the Maui island plan, by pausing increasing transient accommodations and tourism. ”
However, Maui Island Plan section 4.2.3 only provides an aspirational objective and not a
mandate:
Objective 4.2.3 states: “Maximize residents’ benefits from the visitor industry, a.
Promote a desirable island population by striving to not exceed an island-wide
visitor population of roughly 33 percent of the resident population.”
Thus, Bill 148 is not rationally related to a legitimate state interest as Maui Island Plan
4.2.3 is unenforceable. In addition, the bill is not factually justified as the number of
hotel rooms has declined over that last twenty years and are built in areas designated for
hotel use. See, e.g., New Jersey Shore Builders ’n v. Township Committee of Dover
Tp., 468 A.2d 742 (N.J. 1983) (holding that a moratorium on issuance of building pemiits
Pacific Guardian Center ● Makai Tower ● 733 Bishop Street, Suite 2900 ● Honolulu, Hawaii 96813
Phone: 808,599.9555 ● Fax: 808.533.2467 ● www.SMLhawaii.com
Mayor Michael P. Victorino
1/6/22
Page 3
for conslruclion ofmulti-family housing and for conversion of motels into condominiums
was invalid due to lack of factual justification for moratorium in regard to problems of
water supply and water pressure and explaining that “[t]he situation must be exigent, the
causes must be adequately explored, and it must be demonstrated that other less extreme
solutions have been investigated and found to be not feasible. None of these requisite
proofs is before the court. Stripped to its essentials, the ordinance is nothing more than an
expedient legislative reaction”)-
Note that Maui residents would have standing to challenge the bill as a violation of their
procedural due process rights because the Council side-stepped the Charter process to
weaponize the effect of Maui Island Plan section 4.2.3 and thus, denied the public’s role.
And of course, hotels that have pending applications before the Planning Commission
have standing to challenge the bill as a violation of Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth
Amendment.
Even if the Council characterized the moratorium as a revision to the general plan,
Charter section 8-8.6 requires referral to the Planning Commission and if it disapproves
of the proposed revision or fails to make its report with 120 days, the Council could only
pass such revision by affirmative vote of at least two thirds of the Council’s entire
membership.
Very truly yours,
SULLIVAN MEHEULA LEE, LLLP
William Meheula
Pacific Guardian Center ● Makai Tower ● 733 Bishop Street, Suite 2900 ● Honolulu, Hawai'i 96813

From:

COUNTY CLERK
Aloha Councilmembers:
Maui County needs to own the EMI water delivery system.
This is an opportunity to create a crown jewel in the future of Maui Island.
Entities like A&B or Mahi Pono's pension fund owner or Trinitas care about profits and water is
about people. Sadly, in today's world, it's unrealistic to expect them to restore the water shed to
a productive state or to spend budget to update the system so water is not lost in transport.
As long as these corporations have their profit needs met, other needs such as cultural needs are
ignored. That's a fact with 100 years of experience. This fact is a cornerstone for the reason to
buy and operate the EMI.
Costs will be discussed as if they are a stumbling block or a burden. The Water Dept is sitting on
a multi-million dollar fund that has not been used for building reservoirs, transmission lines,
etc. Those dollars along with delivery charges and possibly a bond will pay for the acquisition and
pay for the entire system to be upgraded.
Maui Island water is as pure as any water in the world. An updated system that provides
abundant water for cultural farming, stream life and all other island needs is an act that all citizens
will support and be grateful about.
Maui has many jewels...owning our water delivery system makes all of Maui's jewels sparkled a
more brightly.
Mahalo for your unending efforts on behalf of the citizens and the Aina.
Bill Greenleaf
Greenleaf Farm

Concerning Bill 148 and County Communication 22-9
We are in support of reversing the Veto set in place by our mayor.
We support Bill 148 which will set a moratorium on new Transient Accommodations on Maui, and pause further
development of new hotels, timeshares, short-term rental homes, and transient vacation rental units, for two years
or until tourism management measures are implemented.
We have lived in the islands for 32 years and of course change is inevitable, but it has become disturbing how many
tourists do arrive, many respectful but many not.
Just shopping has become a plan your timing event. In these covid times, it already is extra difficult. I went to a store
the other day, very early to beat the rush of folks getting of planes to do their shop, and I was the only person in line
for the checkout. A tourist (it was obvious) comes and stands 2 feet behind me, not respecting the six-foot rule at all.
wearing a mask below the nose.
Traffic has become much worse in the last several years and there is not enough good and affordable housing for
residents.
Please reconsider the reinstatement of Bill 148.
Thank you,

IYou don't often get email from molly@mollyjacobson.com. Learn why this is important
Aloha Maui County Council Members:
I am writing in support of the moratorium on visitor accommodations on Maui that was passed by the
County Council and then vetoed by Mayor Victorino.
This moratorium has the will of the people behind it, and I urge you to forge ahead and stand by your
original vote and OVERRIDE his veto.
We must start regulating tourism more closely, because the unregulated OVER tourism we currently have
is killing the golden goose.
We run the risk of not only damaging our own wellbeing and safety and way of life, but also losing the
very income people like Mayor Victorino hope to protect.
I used to write restaurant reviews for a tourist-oriented book that was the second-best-selling book about
Maui travel (after the ridiculous monster Maui Revealed). As such, I am a member of multiple Facebook
groups aimed at tourists coming to Maui specifically.
Over the years since 2008, when I first joined Facebook, I have seen a MARKED decline in opinion about
Maui as a destination. Folks who used to come every year now skip a few years because "it's so crowded
now."
People who come are less interested in the culture than in the "tourist attractions." They don’t seem to
understand that this isn't a tourist attraction, it's an island, home to many people, and a beautiful place to
VISIT.
They think it's made for them, not open to them.
And that is driving kind, respectful visitors away. The cheaper the vacation, the more people come -- this is
basic supply and demand economics.
The addition of dozens of direct flights is sometimes blamed, but I think we all know that the main driver
of over-tourism is the number of beds available on the island.
Quite simply, when we started letting people rent out their homes and condos to visitors, we opened up
the floodgates. And the more hotels that have sprung up, the worse it gets.
1
I have written in the past about the need to regulate tourism on Medium.com. Just in case you missed
them:
https://mollyiacobson.medium.com/over-tourism-on-maui-behaves-exactlv-like-cancer-in-the-body-
242ca2ed30d4
https://mollyJacobson.medium.com/in-opposition-to-the-environmental-assessment-for-short-term-
vacation-rentals-for-the-super-rich-188bbe710275
https://mollyJacobson.medium.com/troublina-doubling-how-addina-an-insianificant-332-visitors-per-
day-to-mauis-populatlon-will-b1859d8ecdd8

Over-Tourism on Maui Behaves Exactly
Like Cancer in the Body. | by Molly
Jacobson Medium
THREE: Evading apoptosis ... Not Committing Suicide to
Prevent Harm. Cancer cells grow fast and don't stop.
They also refuse to die. Normal cells are born, live a
certain length of time ... and then kill themselves
naturally and quietly at the end of their natural lifespan.
nnollyjacobson.medium.com
The Maui Island Plan suggests there should never be more than 1 visitor for every 2 residents, and for
good reason. This reasonable — more than reasonable — limit allows the environment to recover, the
infrastructure to stay intact, and the quality of life for residents to remain high.
Any place that has a high quality of life for residents is by definition a lovely place to visit. When life
quality lowers, visitor experience lessens as well.
Just like the proverbial frog boiled alive, the pandemic has shown us all just how hot the water is on Maui.
In 2019, most of us were alarmed at the number of visitors we had. The next year with its sudden decrease
was shocking, not only because we remembered Just how lovely this island is, but also because the
promises made to us were not kept.
We were told by leaders that protecting the island from over-tourism was a goal and that once tourism
resumed, we would see measures taking place to do so.
And then in October of 2020, the promises were forgotten. The number of tourists we are now
experiencing is threatening everything we hold dear, including our environment, wildlife, and our own
health and safety.
I don't need to lecture you about how fragile our infrastructure is. I know you know firsthand how bad our
sewage treatment systems are, our water shortages, the reefs dying, and the landfill that will be full within
a year or two.
Meanwhile, the tourists who are flooding our beaches are chasing dolphins and seals and honu with
impunity. Our fisherman have to go farther out to catch and are crowded off the beaches, which means
they have to feed their families from their wallets, not their tackle box.
Mayor Victorino has shown himself to be completely in the pocket of business interests, and his veto
reflects that.
3
He clearly does not value the long-term health and wellbeing of the island over the short-term interests of
tourism business owners. As a business owner, I am all for a healthy economy, but a healthy economy
does NOT consist of just one industry. We urgently need a way to diversify the economy so that "all boats
can rise."
A moratorium on future visit accommodations will at least give a pause to the industry and allow us to
organize efforts to help create better solutions than Just more of the same.
This is a common-sense moratorium, and I urge you to override his veto. I am very disappointed in the
Mayor's efforts to hold back the tide of public opinion/will, and I will support someone else — someone
who puts residents over tourists — in the next election.
I appreciate and respect the Council and the current members. It is very difficult to take on the leadership
roles you have been elected to. There are many competing interests to weigh and consider, and no
solution is ever perfect.
But this solution — not letting the tourism industry expand the number of beds on this island so we can all
catch our breath -- is about as perfect as it gets.
Please, override the Mayor's veto.
Molly Jacobson
Kihei

Bill 148 County Communication 22-9 Moratorium on Transient Accommodations

IYou don't often get email from dotjakubek@gmaii.com. Learn why this is important
Good Morning Maui County Council Members,
I am writing to show that I support the moratorium on visitor/transient accommodations that was passed by the County
Council and vetoed by Mayor Victorino. I request that you override his veto. This moratorium is needed to help in
controlling the over-tourism that is currently a very large issue on the islands. Why is it that the developers and large
hotel companies are dictating what happens on the islands? Why is it that greed is all I see on the islands? Why is it that
we do not continue to try to preserve the beauty of the islands? Why is it that the Real Estate companies are getting
rich off of the islands? And the local people are now being forced out of their homes and can not or will not be able to
afford to live on the islands that are rightfully theirs.
1 know that I have brought up this fact to you all before, but should we really be continuing to bring more and more
people to the islands at one time? It used to be that this was a special place to come to, a place where you could be
thankful to come to. The idea that you would encourage more people to come and then brag about the amount of
tourists that we have on island at any given time is plain and simple, nuts. The traffic is horrible on any given day and
when there is an accident or flooding or fire, everything comes to a complete shut down. Why? Because we really only
have one real road that goes from the West side to the other side of the island. How dangerous and how frustrating for
those that work or live on one side or the other. Not to mention how critical it is when someone is in need to get to the
hospital and be stuck on the West side stuck in traffic around the Pali. We sat for 3 hours one day trying to get back
home from Kahului because a line was down over the road.
The infrastructure of this island should be your main concern before you keep thinking about bringing in more and more
people. The water/waste issue should be your main concern before you allow more buildings to be erected. Not to
mention the amount of people here versus the size of our hospital or the amount of staff that we still have at our
hospital in recent days. What happened to our second hospital plans?
The people of Hawaii should be your main concern before you keep destroying their beautiful islands and jamming all of
this over everything at them. Stop and think and study what is happening here. Do not be so quick to allow more
before we take care of our own issues. Why keep ruining such beauty.
Thank you for the opportunity to share my thoughts.
Mahalo,
C T3

Dorothy

Testimony on Bill 148 County Communication 22-9 Moratorium on Transient

From:

IYou don't often get email from kelly.jakubek@gmail,com. Learn why this is important
January 6, 2022
Aloha Members of Maui County Council,
I am writing to offer my support for the moratorium on Visitor and Transient Accommodations passed by the County
Council, and unfortunately vetoed by Mayor Victorino. I respectfully ask that you do the right thing and override the
Mayor's veto. With this moratorium, you can help reign in Maui’s worsening over-tourism-which is severely impacting
resident's quality of life, causing damage to the land, and diverting resources and housing away from residents.
Tourism numbers are beginning to exceed pre-pandemic levels. This kind of growth is unsustainable and is wreaking
havoc to our natural resources-ie. abuse and damage of hiking areas, beaches, and parks. I am disappointed in Mayor
Victorino for vetoing this moratorium and failing to protect the well-being and best interests of residents. The Mayor has
not only chosen to align with unregulated businesses that continue to cause severe congestion on our roadways, take
away parking at beaches, and deplete the island's resources, but he continues to rally behind mainland investors who
have already driven up housing costs and forced local residents to leave their homes-many who have relocated to the
mainland.
The Maui Island Plan would help provide much needed homes to residents and improve resident access to our island’s
resources, particularly water that has been diverted away from residents to resorts (to fill their pools and maintain their
landscaping).
I urge the Maui council to take action to do what's best for our land and its residents and override the Mayor's veto.
Respectfully,
Kelly Jakubek

RECEiVEDPRMA
Ml JAN -6 R-1 4: 19V ♦ ♦ ♦Cho-^
January 6, 2022 OFFICE OF THE
COUNTY CLEF^K
Dear Maui County Councilmembers,
On behalf of Maui PRMA, the Vacation Rental Trade Council under the Maui Chamber of Commerce,
we would like to ask you to uphold the Mayor's veto of the proposed moratorium on transient
accommodations. Bill 148 establishing chapter 19.98.
PRMA, the Professional Rental Management Association, is a coalition of professional property
management companies representing over 1600 legally zoned condominium vacation rental
units throughout Maui. Our members are licensed in the State of Hawaii, engaged in the
management of legal vacation rental properties, primarily condominiums, and comply with real
estate license law and code of ethics. Our companies represent 216 years in business, employing
nearly 200 employees and over 300 independent contractors and vendors.
The visitor industry supports so many other small businesses, contributing to our island's overall
economic health. When this industry is stifled and suffers, jobs are lost and that creates broad waves
of negative impacts that ripple throughout our community. When our industry was shut down during
COVID, West Maui in particular saw unemployment rates in the 50%+ range with food lines that were
2-3 hours long. Changes to our industry affect our local community, especially in the areas
where many of the tourism related employees live and reside (West/South Maui).
We agree with the Mayor in that ultimately, this moratorium will not stop visitors from traveling to
Maui. We believe it will have other negative impacts such as an increase in illegal units at a time when
we are trying to support legal vacation rentals and shut down illegal operations. We would support
continued efforts in allowing permitted transient accommodations to apply and operate in order to
continue to collect GET & TAT revenue and reduce the number of illegal operators. If there is no
means for homeowners interested in pursuing legal permits, we run the risk of creating more
illegal operators. At the end of the two years, this moratorium may create a bigger problem
than when it started.
On behalf of PRMA, we ask that you would NOT overturn the Mayor's veto. Thank you for your
consideration and we welcome any discussion with you or a member of your administration and we
can be contacted at Mauiprma@gmail.com.
Mahalo,
John Kevan
Angela Leone
Co-Founders of Maui Professional Rental Management Association fMaui PRMA1

The Moratorium on New Transient Accommodations
From:
Sent:
To: OFFICE OF THb
OUNTY CLERKSubject:
IYou don’t often get email from mauimanokane@yahoo.com. Learn why this is important
Aloha e Members of the County Council,
1 am still in favor of the moratorium on new transit accommodations and urge you to override the
Mayor's veto.
There are plenty of hotels of various sizes, prices, and amenities on Maui.* Seldom are any of them
"sold out."
Figures from the Hawaii Tourism Authority show that even in pre-pandemic 2019, Maui's average
occupancy was in the low 80% range. The November 2021 average was up to 79%.
Thus, there are plenty of rooms to rent and there is no indication the island need more hotels.
Finally, this is a moratorium, not a law carved in granite. Should the day come when more hotel
rooms are needed on Maui (doubtful), the Council can suspend the moratorium for short periods of
time, as needed.
Please override the Mayor's veto.
Respectfully,
Marty Martins
KThei

COUNTY CLERKFROM: Painting Industry of Hawaii Labor Management Cooperation Trust Fund
Hawaii Tapers Market Recovery Trust Fund
Hawaii Glaziers, Architectural Metal Glassworkers Local Union 1889 AFL-CIO Stabilization Trust Fund
Carpet, Linoleum and Soft Tile Local Union 1926 Market Recovery Trust Fund
RE: Bill 148 (2021) MORATORIUM ON NEWVISITORACCOMMODATIONS
Meeting Date: January 7, 2022
Dear Chair Lee and Council Members;
Thank you for this opportunity to submit testimony on behalf of the Painting Industry of Hawaii Labor
Management Cooperation Trust Fund; Hawaii Tapers Market Recovery Trust Fund; Hawaii Glaziers,
Architectural Metal Glassworkers Local Union 1889 AFL-CIO Stabilization Trust Fund; and the Carpet, Linoleum
and Soft Tile Local Union 1926 Market Recovery Trust Fund in strong opposition to Bill 148 (2021). The
foregoing organizations are labor management cooperation funds between the Painters Union, Tapers Union,
Glaziers Union, and Carpet and Soft Tile Layers Union and their signatory contractors. I am a compensated
lobbyist.
In its current form. Bill 148 (2021) completely ignores the recommendations of the Maui Planning Commission
and places the future livelihoods of our members who live and work on Maui (approximately 200 members
across the four trades) in jeopardy at the worst possible time. Imagine how you might be affected if you were not
able to draw a paycheck for over two years. This measure, which claims that is intended to improve the lives of
Maui residents could actually force local residents to leave the island or state for lack of jobs in the future and will
likely adversely affect the economy in the form of lower tax revenue from construction and tourism.
Moreover, this measure will very likely result in negative consequences for the community. As Mayor Victorino
noted in vetoing the bill, tourists were not deterred from travel to Maui by the lack of rental vehicles or
accommodations. What will likely happen if this measure passes is an increase in the use of legal and illegal
vacation rentals, which will only drive up the cost of housing for local residents even further.
Overriding Mayor Victorino's veto and passing this measure would be a serious mistake, and we respectfully ask
that you do not vote to override the veto. Thank you for this opportunity to testify.
Very truly yours,
Jeffrey Masatsugu

January 5, 2022
Aloha [COUNCILMEMBERL
We, a coalition of tourism, business, and labor organizations, are appealing to you to request
your consideration in voting to sustain Maui Mayor Michael Victorino's veto of Bill 148, \A/hich would
create a moratorium on the issuance of building permits for all new lodging accommodations
throughout Maui. We are aware and concerned about the intent of the measure that was passed by the
Maul County Council. We believe strongly that Bill 148, as it is currently written, will not have the
intended effects sought by the Council and will inadvertently hurt not only Maui's overall tourism
industry but also have adverse consequences for countless other businesses that rely on tourism to
employ thousands of Maui residents.
For instance. Bill 148 does not adequately address the proliferation of illegal, short-term
vacation rental units—an issue that begs for more attention and prioritization. As we are all well aware,
the most explosive growth in visitor accommodations in recent years has not been in the traditional,
brick-and-mortar lodging operations, which have been nominal, but in short-term vacation rental
units—both legal and illegal. Unscrupulous operation of illegal units has led to the unchecked growth of
short-term rental inventory in both resort and residential zoned areas. Ease of booking, relative price,
and availability have drawn budget travelers to these units. This will continue and likely worsen if the
development of traditional lodging properties is limited. Curtailing development and restricting growth
will only drive more visitors to these accommodations and will further exacerbate the need for more
affordable housing for local residents.
It also remains our position that a moratorium on building permits will have the unintended
effect of depressing the market for other sectors of the economy, including the construction industry
and other various skilled trades—many of which rely upon the tourism industry for their economic well
being. The issuance of building permits ultimately means more projects, more jobs, and more
opportunities for Maui residents; limiting this for our economy on the heels of a worldwide pandemic is
self-destructive and will have lasting economic consequences for Maui County. Meaningful and
substantive investment into Maui's economy could be jeopardized or lost.
It is a substantive fact that tourism remains Maui's strongest economic driver. It consistently
provides jobs not only in the lodging industry but also in ground and air transport, activities and
1 I MHLA
attractions, retail and dining, the service industry, and the agricultural sector, which provides local goods
and produce for eateries enjoyed by visitors and residents alike. Putting a two-year hold on building
permits will effectively hamstring the industry as it works to attract the ideal traveler and provide a
quality experience on the Valley Isle, hurting our overall tourism product and creating new challenges
and roadblocks that will need to be addressed in the future.
Finally, we would be remiss not to cite the last-minute changes that were made to Bill 148 just
prior to its passage. This did not allow for proper vetting and for a robust public discussion to take place.
A measure with such staggering impacts on the local populace and economy deserves more openness
and transparency, and this measure was not given the appropriate time to be considered by the public
in any meaningful way.
In closing, we would like to reiterate that we understand that the people of Maui are seeking
well-thought-out solutions to strike a balance between the needs and desires of local residents and
visitors. We remain steadfast in our belief that Bill 148 is not the answer. We, therefore, stand ready to
work with the Maui County Council to identify alternate strategies to address better tourism
management, so at this time, we ask that you consider the ramifications of this measure and vote to
sustain Mayor Victorino's veto.
Mahalo, for your consideration,
(Signatures on following pages)

TO: Councilmember Alice Lee, Chair
Councilmember Keani Rawlins-Fernandez, Vice- Chair
Members of the Maui County Council
CD
FR: AMERICAN RESORT DEVELOPMENT ASSOCIATION - HAWAII (ARDA-Hawaii)
RE: Support of to CC 22-9 (Mayor notifying of Veto of Bill 148 entitled "A Bill for an
Ordinance Establishing Chapter 19.98, Maui County Code, Declaring A Moratorium on
New Transient Accommodations on Maui")
Hearing date: Friday, January 7, 2022 at 9:00AM
Aloha Chair Lee, Vice Chair Rawlins-Fernandez and members of the Maui County Council,
Thank you for allowing ARDA-Hawaii to submit testimony in STRONG SUPPORT of CC 22-9
regarding a veto of Bill 148 establishing Chapter 19.98, Maui County Code, declaring a
moratorium on new transient accommodations on Maui. Bill 148 seeks to create an island wide
moratorium which temporarily prohibits the issuance of any permit under Title 19. The proposed
measure creates multiple concerns that could have broad impacts on Maui’s economy.
The stated purpose of the proposed bill is to establish a moratorium to comply with visitor to
resident ratio specified in Chapter 2.SOB of the Maui Island Plan by pausing the increase of
transient accommodations. However, there is no data to suggest that stopping the development of
transient accommodations will decrease the number of visitors to Maui. It is simple, it won’t.
Visitors will still come to Maui and seek other accommodations even if the supply of lodging units
is limited. ARDA Hawaii agrees with the Mayor that as a result of the moratorium the volume of
visitors will permeate into the residential neighborhoods and long-term apartment inventory on
Maui through an increase in short-term vacation rentals ("STR"), which represent the fastest-
growing segment within Maui's visitor accommodations industry. If the purpose of the bill is to
ultimately decrease the visitor count, perhaps further regulation is needed on the number of illegal
short-term vacation rental units. There are better alternatives to accomplish the Council's goals of
reducing the impacts of the tourism industry on Maui residents, without the negative economic
impacts created by the proposed moratorium. Regulating the fastest growing segment of transient
accommodations in Maui by enforcing existing rules against illegal STRs, would provide the
greatest reduction in visitors to comply with the Maui Island Plan.
1
Conversely, the moratorium would seek to limit transient accommodations island wide, thus,
prohibiting increased accommodations even in districts that are intended for tourism. Hotel and
resort areas are where visitor accommodations should be focused and that aids aid in insulating
Maui residents from the perceived negative impacts of tourism.
In addition, ARDA Hawaii agrees with the Mayor's concerns with the insufficient opportunity for
the public to weigh in on the amendments made at second reading. At the previous council hearing,
several amendments were made to Bill 148 without first being posted with the agenda. The public
was deprived of the opportunity to weigh in on the amendments due to insufficient notice. This is
significant as one of the amendments altered the proposed affordable housing exception ratio for
the moratorium which was an express recommendation made by the Planning Commission.
Further, there are several legal concerns as the proposed moratorium may be unconstitutional as
it: I) fails to substantially advance a legitimate government interest as required by the due process
clause; 2) is unconstitutionally vague; 3) and violates the equal protection clause in treating
similarly situated property owners differently.
Bill 148 also unfairly impacts existing projects currently undergoing permit application review.
Section 2 as currently drafted makes the moratorium applicable to permits currently being
reviewed that have not received their final discretionary approval. This amendment to Section 2 is
patently unfair to applicants who have already expended significant resources and time to obtain
a permit that is being reviewed. Further, Section  2would directly contradict the Planning
Commission recommendation that the moratorium does not affect current permit applications.
Moreover, the moratorium will have substantial economic impacts on Maui’s economy. It is
concerning that the County would seek to deter capital investment in a time where it is still
recovering from the pandemic. This is especially problematic given the recent surge in cases that
may continue to impact the tourism industry. The County would risk forgoing substantial amounts
of investments, tax revenues and Job creation for Maui’s economy. For example, the timcshare
industry is currently a major contributor to Maui’s economy by providing more than $73 million
per year in state and local taxes, providing occupancies which keep Maui residents employed and
supplying well compensated jobs to Maui residents.
Further, as the association representing the vacation ownership and resort development industries
in Hawaii, ARDA-Hawaii is surprised that the County would want to stop timeshare visitors from
coming to Maui. The timeshare visitor has the exact profile of the type of visitor that we should
welcome with higher income levels, and more spending off property in restaurants and local stores,
and who are more likely to take care of their property and Maui County. Maui is a “home away
from home" as timeshare visitors are owners, not transients. We should be mindful that the
timeshare industry could be part of the solution.
The proposed ordinance would enact a moratorium until the Council enacts legislation
implementing recommendations by the Tourism Management Temporary Investigative Group
("TIG") which establishes limits on accommodation types and area. This poses significant risk to
Maui’s economy, without first obtaining information to better manage the industry. Instead, the
2
TIG, in collaboration with the tourism industry, could address the Council’s concerns prior to any
moratorium being implemented to prevent causing unnecessary harm to Maui’s fragile economy,
which is still recovering from the pandemic.
Additionally, the proposed ordinance is intended to mitigate negative impacts on the environment
and residents’ quality of life. As has been stated many times, there is a lack of data suggesting that
a moratorium will substantially reduce the negative impacts on the environment or residents. It is
concerning that such a broad and inflexible policy would be implemented without first showing
transient accommodations as the primary cause of these negative impacts. As mentioned
previously, further regulation of illegal STRs would reduce the negative impacts on resident's
quality of life without implementing such an inflexible policy that would result in lost jobs and
reduced economic activity for residents.
As emphasized by the Mayor, due consideration should be given to the broader impacts of the
proposed measure. We as a community should consider a resolution that provides Maui residents
with the ability to continue to work and provide for their families, while at the same time
addressing the impacts of the influx of visitors, until Maui can transition to a more diversified
economic base.
I respectfully ask that the Council uphold the Mayor’s veto of Bill 148 and instead pursue the
further regulation of illegal STRs prior to implementing any form of moratorium to address the
Council's concerns in a more meaningful way.
Thank you for your consideration of my comments.
Respectfully submitted,
Ryan Nobriga
Maui Task Force Chair
ARDA Hawaii
