RE: Bill 148, County Communication 22-9
Moratorium on Transient Accommodations
Email: county.cIerk@mauicounty.us
Dear Maui County Council Members:
As a new physician recruit on Maui (who was recruited to improve the medical care here), 1 am writing this
letter in support of the moratorium on visitor accommodations on Maui, that was passed by the County
Council and vetoed by Mayor Victorino. PLEASE override his veto! This moratorium is a crucial step toward
remediating the current unregulated over-tourism we are seeing.
The Maui Island Plan suggests limiting the number of visitors to approximately 1/3 the number of residents in
order to preserve our environment, infrastructure, and quality of life for residents-all of which would
improve the visitor experience as well.
The year 2019 was already a year of uncontrolled growth, fueled by the tourism industry. Promises were
made by leaders during the early part of the pandemic to improve on the tourism experience for both visitors
and residents. Residents were promised that the goal would be to decrease the number of tourists while
protecting the islands. Since October of 2020, those promises have been completely forgotten by our leaders,
who proudly announce that the goal of reaching 2019 numbers has been met and now exceeded.
The current volume of tourists we were seeing pre-pandemic and now, in 2021, during the pandemic, is a
threat to the health, safety and quality of life of the residents of Maui, our environment and wildlife.
Our island resources are very limited. Our inadequate sewage treatment, water, and landfills are not meant
for this excessive level of use. We just finished months of a severe water shortage, yet only the Upcountry
residents were affected, and not tourists. The hotels are literally sucking up water as if there is no restriction.
While sewage is discharged into our oceans, tourists are overcrowding our beaches and abusing our wildlife
and injuring the reefs.
On Maui, tourists drive all over the island, causing huge traffic congestion—and this is despite the rental car
shortage. Tourists don’t even think twice about using up resources meant for residents, such as UHauls.
The mayor has not shown any desire to control tourism (i.e. vetoing the last proposed moratorium for south
and west Maui and vetoing the affordable housing bill) Mayor Victorino goes out of his way to please the big
money brought in by the tourism industry and mainland investors, He has made it clear that residents are
second class citizens to the first class tourists. It is the responsibility of government officials to ensure that
there is adequate affordable housing for those who are essential to making our community work [health care
professionals, teachers, police, social workers, restaurant workers, grocery/retail workers and yes, workers in
tourism), not to incentivize nonresidents' profiting off tourism.
1
Residents sacrifice a great deal financially to live here and deserve to enjoy the beaches, hikes and parks.
Instead, there is no room for residents on any of these. The majority of residents here do not depend at all on
the tourist industry—yet all of us are made to sacrifice for it. Hardworking residents are trying not to be
chased out by greedy leaders who put short-term profit first.
Our economy needs to be diversified. Our children need to be taught skills that will help them to succeed in
society, rather than just to serve tourists. We need a moratorium on future visitor accommodations while
solutions can be implemented, including leadership that supports resident lives over the tourism industry.
Residents are SO tired of having to write letters again and again and testify again and again for something
that seems so common sense. I am so disappointed in the Mayor, who despite being a Maui native, obviously
supports the tourism industry over our quality of life.
Personally, I can say that unless this passes, I will not continue to live and serve the community here on Maui.
I'm tired of having to hide in my home to avoid the masses of Covid infected visitors while the visitors trample
through the island without wearing their masks. I’m heart sick that this beautiful culture is being sold out to
money. I truly hope someone with integrity steps forward to make these necessary changes.
Sincerely,
Terry E.Restivo, DO
Restivo Plastic Surgery-Maui
85 Maui Lani Parkway
Wailuku, HI 96793
Office:(888)533-2133
Fax:(855)827-2321
2
WHICH TAKE AWAY THE QUALITY OF LIFE AND THE ENVIRONMENT WHICH IS THE
REASON TOURIST STARTED COMING IN THE FIRST PLACE.
I WORK IN THE TOURIST INDUSTRY AND I PERSONALLY HEAR THIS FROM
TOURISTS.
I urge you to NOT stand with Mayor Victorino and vote to sustain his veto of Bill 148. WE

Re: Strong Opposition to Bill 148, Moratorium on New Transient Accommodations on Maui,
and Request to Sustain Veto
Dear Chair Lee and Councilmembers,
The International Union of Bricklayers and Allied Crafts, Local 1, writes to continue its
opposition of Bill 148, which proposes a moratorium on new transient accommodations on
Maui, and humbly requests that the Council not override the Mayor’s veto.
Our members would be dramatically and detrimentally affected by the proposed moratorium. Due to
the discerning nature of Maui’s visitors, hotel construction and renovations typically involve a
substantial amount of high-quality, high-finish stone, marble, terrazzo, and tile work - the type of
work that our well-equipped contractors and well-trained members perform. Hotel construction and
renovation work provides our members with living wage jobs so they can support their families on
Maui County.
If the proposed moratorium were to go into effect, our members and contractors would find it nearly
impossible to find stable and economically-sustaining work opportunities in Maui County. While the
moratorium purports to only be in effect for a few years, if our Maui members are forced to move
way from the island, it will be much more difficult for them to return home afterwards even if hotel
construction were to be permitted again. If local contractors close up shop and are unable to open
back up after the moratorium expires, the void will be filled by mainland contractors which would
further harm the local economy.
With the tourism industry in a tenuous position due to the COVID-19 pandemic and with an
uncertain future ahead for the local construction industry due to the state of the global economy, we
remain extremely concerned by this proposal.
Sincerely,
/s/ Jt.
Melvin P. Silva, Jr.
Business Manager/Financial Secretary-Treasurer
LOCAL nHUiaAC
Some of our members hard at work at the “Maui Bay Villas” project in Kihei late last year. If the
moratorium were to pass, this type of work would not be available to them for years.
,:r
Benjamin Austria, Mario Bstrada, and Michael Cockett Michael Cockett demonstrates his attention to detail
Joey Magsayo and Preston Latu Mario Estrada carefully lays out stone decking near the pool
Elmer Bonilla shares a jobsite shaka Roy Lokosuka and Aisea Lao with BMK, hard at work

Dear Council Members,
Ag Working Group supports CM Shane Sinenci’s resolution to buy the East Maui Irrigation
Aqueduct System and sign the lease for the benefit of Maui’s people.
Ag Working Group has been meeting and discussing the continual lack of reliable water
resources for Maui’s farmers and ranchers for over ten years. We have had numerous
meetings with Department of Water Supply directors and staff over those 10 years. In one
meeting with then Water Department director Dave Taylor, he told us it would cost over $350
million to build a reservoir large enough to serve the needs of upcountry. If this is true then
you must see the purchase of the EMI system and associated lease as a bargain at twice
the price,
if you review the documentation attached to CM Sinenci’s resolution you will see that in 1961
the Board of Supervisors for Maui County unanimously agreed even then that it was a good
idea for the County to have control of the EMI water and used terms like “immediate solu
tion,” “necessary” and “should.”
This was their concluding paragraph written over 60 years ago...
“There is adequate water for all concerned; however, no one party should control its sale
or usage as to be detrimental to others. The County being a subdivision of the State should
have as much rights to the usage of State water as the present licensee. Water is the basic
natural resource necessary for economic development and growth of the island and should
not be controlled as to prevent new development.”
And that is as true now as it was then! More so!
What do you think their opinion would have been if the entity poised to control that resource
was a foreign owned corporation?
We have a catastrophic lack of affordable housing on Maui island. This can be directly tied
to the Fixture unit limitations imposed by DWS. With adequate water resources homeown
ers, farmers and ranchers could upgrade their meters to facilitate building accessory dwell
ings, labor housing and irrigation systems. Our farmers and ranchers reduce their crop and
herd sizes every year because even though our island is one of the wettest locations on the
planet Earth we have no guarantee of water during our most critical time of year - harvest
season.
Please stop kicking the can down the road and secure Maui’s water future!
Reso 22-4
Take on the responsibility for the East Maui Irrigation Aqueduct System and secure a 30 year
lease for our water! The Ag Working Group wholeheartedly supports this investment in our
future! oo XIOm
Sydney Smith, facilitator, Ag Working Group
Maliko Estate Coffee, 808-268-3646 call/text

Regarding the Mayor's veto of Bill 148, my biggest concern is
WATER
- In 2016 when I asked the Maui Water Department to be put on the waiting list for a water meter, I was told "There
is no waiting list."
- During the increasingly frequent droughts many Olinda residents on catchment have had to have water trucked in.
- The Water Dept mails restriction notices to Kula residents almost annually, recently threatening fines for non-
compliance. Kula farmers were given a three month grace period and then were expected to comply with the restriction
mandate. Farmers have to bite the bullet while developers tap into our limited resources for the benefit of non
residents.
- Why hasn't the County upgraded our water system to keep up with demand? Until this issue is resolved a
moratorium on construction of new visitor accommodations is just plain common sense.
-1 urge the Council to override the Mayor's veto and pass Billl48. Until such time as Maui's water system has been
updated to accommodate our current residential and agricultural needs, it is folly to add to the demand.

Aloha Maui County Council Members,
I am writing this letter in support of the moratorium on \dsitor accommodations on Maui that was
passed by the County Council and vetoed by Mayor Victorino.
Please override his veto.
As a full time resident of Maui I ask that you consider the voices of the residents who have been
asking for tourism management for the last two years. Victorino’s veto is doing the exact opposite. I
live in South Kihei and the traffic along South Kihei road is congested on a daily basis.
The increase in visitors has also resulted in an increase of accidents and ocean rescues which is a
drain on emergency resources. I see and hear rescue helicopters, coast guard, and emergency vehicles
daily from my lanai (facing Kamaole 3).
The influx in tourism since we opened up in October 2020 has adversely affected the quality of lives of
Maui residents. From prolonged water restrictions, increased traffic, and jostling -with tourists while
going about our daily chores. Meanwhile, the resorts in Wailea are all operating with multiple
swimming pools and thousands of hotel rooms filled to the brim.
The pandemic has also demonstrated that Hawaii’s reliance on tourism is not only risky, it is outright
irresponsible. When it’s not cheap to live here, Hawaii should not be a cheap place to \dsit. Mass
tourism being encouraged by rock bottom airfares only seive to cheapen Hawaii’s reputation while
doing harm to the quality of life of local residents, the ecosystem, and the environment, not to
mention an incredible drain on our resources.
The over reliance on tourism to sustain the island’s economy is not a good long term strategy. The
question is not what pandemic will hit next. It is WHEN the next pandemic will hit. And once again, it
will bring Hawaii to its knees when it happens.
The quicker we can diversify from this tourism only strategy, the better we vsill all be.
The fact that local residents have to wiite letters again and again about the same issues and
specifically Victorino’s self-ser\dng interest policies is wrong on so many levels.
1
Once again, I am asking you to please override his veto.
Thank you for reading my letter, I trust you will do the right thing.
To protect the land for future generations and to protect the people from a further eroding quality of
life.
Mahalo.
Luanne Teoh
Kihei, Maui.

support for Bill 148 overriding the Mayor's veto
im M -5 M 7: 48

You don't often get email from mary.trotto@liu.edu. Learn whv this is important
Aloha County Council members,
Thank you for voting for Bill 148 in December.
Now that the Mayor has vetoed this bill, the “ball” is
in your “court’. There is much to be learned about
living on this Island with responsible growth.
Bill 148 is a short term solution to a problem that has been
growing since the 90’s. It is time for all of us to step back,
assess what is good for the Island and its surrounding eco systems.
We are custodians of a billion dollar reef in our near shore waters, we
have a need for affordable housing for our residents, we need to look
at how much water we consume and its availability, what is the cost for maintenance
of our infrastructure and how much trash we create and our ability to deal with it.
Quality of life here on Maui needs to be assessed not just for our residents but
also for our visitors. Visitors to our Island pay large amounts of money to come
to Maui to experience the beauty of Maui, its coastal vistas, sunsets, quality of
the water and quality of its life. Residents and visitors alike need those in county
government
to do the right thing to maintain Maui County as  aplace of beauty.
Affordable housing, traffic issues, and infrastructure maintenance are issues we must
address. Further development of visitor accommodations must be curtailed for a short
time in order to evaluate what we already have and how well what currently exists is being
utilized. The question: What is needed to provide the best quality of life for both our
residents and
our visitors? Do you have an answer?
Thank you for your consideration to vote to override the Mayor’s veto.
With warmest aloha,
Dr Mary Trotto
Kihei Resident

2181 LAUWILIWILI STREET, KAPOLEl, HI 96707 ● (808) 845-7871 ● FAX (808) 682-0906
Jurisdiction: Northern California, Northern Nevada, Utah, Hawaii, and the Mid-Pacific Islands
January 7, 2022
Honorable, Alice Lee, Maui County Council, Chair
Honorable, Keani Rawlins-Fernandez, Maui County Council, Vice Chair
Honorable Members of the Maui County Council
RE: Regarding Maui County Council Communication CC22-9 Mayor, notifying of his veto of Bill 148
(2021), Draft 1, entitled "A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING CHAPTER 19.98, MAUI COUNTY
CODE, DECLARING A MORATORIUM ON NE\A/ TRANSIENT ACCOMODATIONS ON MAUI."
Chair Lee:
My name is Analeseanoa Tuiasosopo and I am the District Representative for Hawaii Operating
Engineers Locai 3. Our union represents the 3000 hardworking unionized members in heavy
engineering site work. We are in support of the mayor's veto and ask that you do NOT override it.
I am aware of and concerned about the intent of the measure that was passed by the
Maui County Council. Our organization strongiy believes that Bill 148, as it is currently written, will not
have the intended effects sought by the Council and will inadvertently hurt not only Maui's overall
tourism industry but also have adverse consequences for countless other businesses that rely on
tourism to employ thousands of Maui residents.
1 also believe a moratorium on building permits will have the unintended effect of depressing the
market for other sectors of the economy, including the construction industry and other various skilled
trades—many of which rely upon the tourism industry for their economic well being. The issuance of
building permits ultimately means more projects, more jobs, and more opportunities for Maui residents;
limiting this for our economy on the heels of a worldwide pandemic is self-destructive and will have
lasting economic consequences for Maui County. Meaningful and substantive investment into Maui's
economy could be jeopardized or lost.
Sincerely,
Analeseanoa Tuiasosopo
District Representative- Hawaii
Hawaii Operating Engineers Local 3

IYou don't often get email from steve.lwilson@yahoo.com. Learn why this is important
With Warmest Aloha to the Maui County Council Members,
I am writing to once again voice my support for the moratorium on visitor accommodations. I believe I speak in concert
with tens of thousands of fellow Maui neighbors and ohana that support the idea of placing a hold on what has been
extraordinary and exponential growth of tourism, especially over the last ten to fifteen years. Each and every year, the
numbers rise and rise in excess of what resources we have to support this incredible explosion of tourism. It simply
cannot be sustainable at this rate. We need time to prepare and deal with it in a responsible way. Our quality of life should
not be second to a numbers game.
By passing this moratorium, we position ourselves to reboot the visitor industry to return Maui to a higher degree of
exclusivity, it allows the existing accommodations venues to catch up and become more competitive for a higher
standard of visitor. By adding more rooms, by allowing more short term rentals, all keeps prices artificially low, allowing
more and more visitors to crowd our small island and to overburden our very limited resources, including water,
wastewater facilities, and our roads. We have residents going years without water, while additional hotels and resorts will
absorb yet even more. The quality of life on Maui has sunken. I see it. My neighbors see it, and I am positive each of
you sees it.
Additionally, we have seen our friends and neighbors struggle to find affordable housing. Many of which, serve the visitor
industry. Adding more hotels and resorts will require hundreds, perhaps thousands of more employees to run these new
facilities, and we must ask ourselves, where are these people going to live? Maui has reached and surpassed total
saturation of the tourist industry. We are now adding more and more concrete just to park cars. Hana highway has
become a nightmare, an endless tourist-train of cars. I reside in Hana. I now shudder to think of driving it now when it
used to be an absolute joy.
Just recently, last summer, the Governor and Mayor made progress to curb tourism. The leaders were successful in
putting into place certain measures to address the over-tourism, and what I speak of are the higher accommodations tax,
the crack down on illegal short-term rentals, a tax incentive to convert short terms to long terms, raising property taxes on
short-term rental properties, and several new licensing requirements for short-term rentals. These are all great measures
that will only be diluted by more hotels and resorts. We cannot back-petal these wonderful advances. We need time to
absorb their effectiveness before we allow more facilities that destroy the quality of life we alt deserve and expect. Maui
tourism will always be present as long as we don't chase visitors away with the blight of over-tourism. That can and has
happened to other favored destinations. Let's not make the same fatal mistakes. We must venture into the future with our
eyes open to also preserve the quality of the visit. We need tourism, but Maui is also positioned to chose them. We need
to protect ourselves and our visitors from over-tourism, or we chance ruining our precious lifestyle and opportunities.
We need to work and build on what we have, not add to it. We need to hone it. We need to perfect it. With a more
exclusive visitor, we will build on that visitor. Consider the mindset that Maui, as a host, and in the realm of the costs of
supporting a visitor, the infrastructure cost is  aconstant per visitor no matter their level of social stature. Each visitor
consumes the same average amount of water, wastewater and treatment facility costs, landfill needs, consumes the same
amount of locally grown foods, same airport facility use, a need for a rental car, and more. There is  adollar number on
each visitor’s head, and it's the same for all. Let’s increase the revenue while reducing the infrastructure costs and
demand. Wouldn't it be nice to position the available rooms to limit tourism, which would effectively raise room rates,
which again would raise pre-taxed revenue, thereby increasing taxable revenue on top of the newly increased tax rate of
the accommodations taxes, all to effect an increase of tax revenue to the County, only to end up paying less to host less
visitors based on a per-visitor cost? The answer is simple. YES. Less burden on natural resources, less wastewater and
treatment, less traffic congestion, more available housing, more available local foods, better quality of life and a better
quality of visit, all with more revenue.
1
Please vote to overturn Mayor Victorino’s veto. It's pono, and what the residents want. Its what each of you really wants.
A better life for us all and for our keiki and their keiki. We ail look to each of you, and to Mayor Victorino, for leadership of
our direction...to represent the wants of the residents, not to represent the wants of visitors. Lets work to build on what we
have and allow a couple of years to see what the recent changes can actually do instead of mindlessly sabotaging them
all. Vote YES for the moratorium.
Steve Wilson
Hana, Maui

January 5, 2022
Aloha Maui County Council Members:
I am writing this letter in support of the moratorium on visitor accommodations on Maui, that was passed by
the County Council and vetoed by Mayor Victorino. PLEASE override his veto! This moratorium is a crucial
step toward remediating the current unregulated over-tourism we are seeing here.
The Maui Island Plan suggests limiting the number of visitors to approximately 1/3 the number of residents in
order to preserve our environment, infrastructure, and quality of life for residents--all of which would
improve the visitor experience as well.
The year 2019 was already a year of uncontrolled growth, fueled by the tourism industry. Promises were
made by leaders during the early part of the pandemic to improve on the tourism experience for both visitors
and residents. Residents were promised that the goal would be to decrease the number of tourists while
protecting the islands. Since October of 2020, those promises have been completely forgotten by our leaders,
who proudly announce that the goal of reaching 2019 numbers has been met and now exceeded.
The current volume of tourists we were seeing pre-pandemic in 2021, during the pandemic, is a threat to the
health, safety and quality of life of the residents of Maui, our environment and wildlife.
Our island resources are very limited. Our inadequate sewage treatment, water, and landfills are not meant
for this level of use. We just finished months of  asevere water shortage, yet only Upcountry residents were
affected, not tourists. While my yard dried up and died due to not watering it, the hotels were literally sucking
up water as if there is no restriction. While sewage is discharged into our oceans, tourists are overcrowding
our beaches and cruelly abusing our wildlife. Our fishing industry is endangered by the abuse the ocean
environment is experiencing.
On Maui, tourists do not stay in the tourist areas, but drive all over the island, causing huge traffic
congestion—and this is despite the rental car shortage. Tourists don't even think twice about using up
resources meant for residents, such as UHauls! I have seen horrific pictures of the road to Hana being blocked
by tourists who choose to park on the road, blocking traffic, because of lack of parking.
Residents are literally being told that we do not count and that the tourism industry is all-powerful. Our
mayor has not shown any support of controlling tourism, including vetoing the last proposed moratorium for
south and west Maui and vetoing the affordable housing bill. He goes out of his way to please the big money
brought in by the tourism industry and mainland investors. He has made it clear that residents are second
class citizens to tourists. It is the responsibility of government officials to ensure that there is adequate
affordable housing for those who are essential to making our community work (health care professionals,
teachers, police, social workers, restaurant workers, grocery/retail workers and yes, workers in tourism), not
to incentivize nonresidents' profiting off tourism.
Residents here sacrifice a great deal financially to live here and deserve to be able to enjoy the beaches, hikes
and parks. Instead, there is no room for residents on any of these. The majority of residents here do not
1
depend at all on the tourist industry—yet all of us are made to sacrifice for it. For me, it is about more than a
financial sacrifice, as this is not only my birthplace but also that of my ancestors. Hardworking residents are
trying not to be chased out by greedy leaders who put short-term profit first.
Our economy needs to be diversified. Our children need to be taught skills that will help them to succeed in
society, rather than just to serve tourists. We need a moratorium on future visitor accommodations while
solutions can be implemented, including leadership that supports resident lives over the tourism industry.
Residents are SO tired of having to write letters again and again and testifying again and again for something
that seems so common-sense. I am so disappointed in our Mayor, who despite being a Maui Boy, so obviously
supports the moneyed tourist industry over residents' quality of life. He has sold us out, and 1 for one will do
all 1 can to ensure that someone who supports residents' quality of life will replace him in the next election.
1 appreciate the members of the Maui County Council greatly. With few exceptions, you are the leaders who
put residents and the ‘aina first.
Mahalo,
Charlene Yoshimura
Ph/Text: 808-344-3245
